Kuroda Case Report Nearing Completion; Japanese Cabinet Likely to Collapse; Responsibility Division Theory Creates Major Political Impact

(Tokyo) The current cabinet's future, the fate of which depends on the review of Justice Minister Oyama's investigation report on the Kuroda case, will be determined by the three elders of the government: Prime Minister Saito, Home Minister Yamamoto, and Finance Minister Takahashi. However, summing up the various reports on the political upheaval, it is said that if the content of the incident reported by Justice Minister Oyama is not only related to the Ministry of Finance, but is also extensive and profound, then the entire cabinet will inevitably resign en masse. It is absolutely impossible to use the responsibility division theory to resolve the matter by only having the Finance Minister resign. Even within the government department, apart from the elders, some cabinet members are also advocating joint resignation from a purely theoretical perspective. Even if the Justice Minister's report advocates the responsibility division theory, the theory of joint resignation is still quite powerful in the general trend. Therefore, the hope for the leadership's life-saving strategy is slim. Justice Minister Oyama's report is scheduled to be submitted on the 25th or 26th, and the atmosphere of a political upheaval will be quite strong at that time. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

(Tokyo) The intentions of the influential figures in the House of Peers regarding the responsibility division theory of Finance Minister Takahashi are generally as follows: Finance Minister Takahashi's reason for advocating the responsibility division theory of the Ministry of Finance incident is to avoid involving other cabinet members and to minimize the impact on the political situation. However, if the malfeasance incident of the suspects in the Ministry of Finance incident is clear, then the current cabinet, which touts rectifying discipline, should quickly express its future. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

(Tokyo) At a time when the current cabinet is standing at the crossroads of continuing or collapsing, Finance Minister Takahashi, whose future is most noteworthy, suddenly issued the responsibility division theory, which has had a great impact on various aspects of the political world. Secretary-General Aso of the Minseito Party told reporters about this matter, saying that the current cabinet should be responsible for the Ministry of Finance incident. Although Finance Minister Takahashi has issued the theory that the responsibility of the Finance Minister for supervision and the responsibility of the Prime Minister can be divided, the current cabinet, which is organized to promote the clearing of discipline, has actually brewed this action of disrupting discipline itself and cannot be at peace. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

(Tokyo) Yesterday, Army Minister Hayashi questioned Justice Minister Oyama, urging Justice Minister Oyama to quickly conclude the Zaibu corruption case. It is said that this was prompted by the Araki faction of the military. It is said that the upper echelons of the Japanese political world are doing their best to avoid a political upheaval because General Ugaki, the most powerful candidate for Prime Minister, has fled back to Keijo after being attacked by the hard-line factions of the army and navy. Baron Hiranuma, who was nominated by the Araki faction, was also attacked by the combined forces of senior statesmen, zaibatsu, and political parties and cannot take office. The other candidates all have their own strengths and weaknesses, making it very difficult to realize. Therefore, they strongly advocate the theory of individual responsibility for the Minister of Finance to avoid a political upheaval. If a political upheaval is unavoidable, then Saito will be pushed up again to avoid major domestic turmoil. It is said that the Fascist faction is threatening Justice Minister Oyama to thoroughly investigate the matter, even to the point of arresting former Education Minister Hatoyama. Their purpose is very clear: to undermine party politics. The inner workings of the political world are very gloomy. (Hualian Telegram, 23rd)

Germany Accepts British Proposal; To Resolve Debt Problems; Will Send Representatives to Great Britain to Open Negotiations

(Berlin) Today, the German government has accepted the British government's proposal to hold negotiations to reach a compromise to resolve Germany's foreign debt troubles. Around Sunday, the German government will send representatives by plane to London to consult with the British government. It is expected that the German government will not propose immediate concessions. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

Anglo-German Dispatches Exchanged; London Publishes White Paper

(London) The documents exchanged between Great Britain and Germany regarding German foreign debt were published as a White Paper today. The wording of the British dispatch is extremely candid, and its sharp tone has raised speculation in business circles about whether this dispatch can promote understanding between the two countries. The financial and political circles do not view the future favorably. When the British dispatch was delivered to Berlin but not yet published, Schacht, the President of the German National Bank, had already issued passionate remarks yesterday.

According to a Berlin telegram, the German National Bank has announced new regulations governing foreign exchange, stipulating that (1) the amount of foreign exchange released each day in the future shall not exceed the amount received, (2) the distribution of demand in various countries shall not be consistent, and priority must be given to the needs of raw materials and food, and (3) all payments of foreign debt must first be submitted to the National Bank for approval (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

(London) This afternoon, the government released a white paper, which includes (1) the German government's note to Great Britain after the German central bank decided to suspend payment of foreign debt principal and interest, and (2) Great Britain's reply to the German government on this matter, which was delivered by the British ambassador to Germany yesterday. The main points of the white paper are that Great Britain invited Germany to send representatives to consult with the British government on Germany's long-term and medium-term debts, government bonds, and the entire issue of debt remittance. The German note of June 15 stated that Germany has no intention of denying its debts. However, because the amount of Germany's foreign debt is too large, Germany must have a surplus in foreign trade in order to repay the principal and interest on its foreign debt. Therefore, the German government has no choice but to reduce the quantity of imports in order to save money to pay for imports that cannot be avoided and to continue remitting foreign debt to the extent possible. The German note finally stated that Germany hopes that various countries will not take retaliatory measures against German exports, which would make Germany's difficult situation even more serious. Foreign Minister Simon's reply stated that British creditors had previously recognized temporary concessions to Germany so that Germany could overcome its difficulties. Various concessions are also being prepared for commercial debts, provided that Germany respects the Dawes and Young loans. Since the interest on the two loans accounts for only 2% of Germany's total income, there is no reason for Germany to refuse to pay. From 1933 to 1934, Anglo-German trade actually benefited Germany, and the amount of money that Germany made from this surplus exceeded three times the interest that Germany had to pay on all bonds issued in London. The reply also stated that the British government has decided to request the necessary powers from Parliament to protect British commercial and financial interests. However, if a compromise can be reached to avoid taking offset measures, Great Britain is still willing to negotiate. Therefore, it hopes that the German government will quickly send representatives to London to conduct negotiations. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

(Paris) According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, if Germany does not pay the principal and interest on the Dawes and Young loans, the French government has decided to take offset measures, that is, to convert the surplus of German trade with France into marks and list it under the German government's deposit account. However, because the principal and interest for the previous period were paid on June 15, and there are no arrears from now until July 15, the above offset measures will not be implemented by the French government until July 15, when France and Germany cannot reach an agreement. (Havas Telegram, 22nd)

German Fleet Visits Great Britain in Return

(Berlin) The German cruisers Königsberg and Leipzig will visit Portsmouth for four days on July 11 in return for the visit of the British destroyers to Swinemünde last week. This is the first time that German warships have entered British ports since the Great War. (National Telegram, 22nd)

Great Britain Boycotts Japanese Goods; Rejects Japanese Request

(Tokyo) Great Britain is ignoring the protest lodged by Ambassador Matsudaira to Great Britain on May 17 regarding the ratio system for Japanese goods, and continues to implement it in the colonies directly under British control, following the policy of its own country. Therefore, on the 21st, Ambassador Matsudaira and Commercial Attaché Matsuyama visited Secretary of State for Trade Hore-Belisha and demanded a reply to the Japanese protest. After stating Great Britain's attitude, Secretary of State for Trade Hore-Belisha replied that Japan's request could not be fully recognized. Therefore, the ratio system for dealing with Japanese goods will continue to be implemented in British colonies in the future. Ambassador Matsudaira and Commercial Attaché Matsuyama will continue to negotiate strongly with Secretary of State for Trade Hore-Belisha to urge him to reconsider. (Dentsu Telegram, 23rd)

International PEN Club Closes; H.G. Wells Re-elected President; Next Congress to be Held in Spain

(London) The International PEN Club Congress, having convened in Edinburgh for three days, announced its closure today after electing H.G. Wells to continue as president for another year. Playwright Mrs. Dawson and poet Walter were elected as permanent members of the Executive Committee. Representatives from Austria, France, England, America, Catalonia, Czechoslovakia, India, and Scotland are all on the Executive Committee. The assembly unanimously voted to hold next year's congress in Catalonia. During today's meeting, representatives from various European countries engaged in heated debates. Initially, Italian author Manitti and the representative from Czechoslovakia, Bilar, clashed. The verbal battle intensified after Bilar made sarcastic remarks. Subsequently, German author Toller proposed a resolution protesting to the German government against the imprisonment of German authors and the burning of their works. Swiss representative Meyer immediately criticized Toller, stating that Toller himself had once harassed authors and journalists. Toller then called Meyer a liar, causing a great uproar in the assembly. Order was eventually restored, and the resolution was passed. German playwright and author Ludwig proposed a resolution stipulating the procedures for convening PEN Club congresses, so that writers worldwide could take joint action in times of war or the threat of war. Wells opposed this proposal, saying that if it were passed, he would resign, believing that such views were merely empty talk and could not be effective, therefore it should not be put to a vote. (Special dispatch from the Zilin News on the 22nd)

U.S. Continues to Purchase Silver

(Washington) Semi-official sources estimate that the U.S. government has purchased approximately 100 million ounces of silver since the start of the silver relief plan. The funds for purchasing the silver come from the exchange equalization fund of 200 million yuan stored in the national treasury. The purchase price ranges from 40 to 50 cents. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau plans to purchase approximately another 130 million ounces of silver to meet the amount stipulated in the silver bill. It is generally intended to continue purchasing in London and New York. The government hopes that the price of silver will increase after the Treasury Department purchases silver, which in turn will increase other commodity prices. (National Telegram on the 22nd)

As a result, striking workers are becoming increasingly vocal and threatening these ships, declaring that they will refuse to load or unload cargo on ships heading to Europe, Australia, and the Atlantic coast. Officials are now preparing to use police to protect the ports in the Northwest region, so that they will not be blockaded by workers. (Havas News Agency dispatch on the 23rd)

Handling Marital Disputes in Bandit Areas

▲ Nanchang Headquarters Formulates Eight Measures

Nanchang Correspondence: The Red Bandits have always advocated breaking down the patriarchal society and promoting communal wives and communal property. In the areas they occupy, rites, customs, and laws are completely destroyed. The relations between men and women are especially chaotic, with absolute freedom of marriage and divorce. The poison has spread so widely that it has almost become promiscuity. Now, as the bandit areas are gradually recovered, refugees return in droves. Some wives have been taken by others, some have been forced to divorce by the bandits and now urgently seek reconciliation, or some couples, due to uncertainty about each other's survival, have temporarily formed relationships with others and now wish to reunite. Even those who were previously drafted by the bandits into laundry and comfort teams, or who were forcibly married by the bandits and have escaped, are numerous. Therefore, there are many disputes arising from marriage and divorce among men and women in the recovered areas. The Headquarters has now specially formulated eight measures for handling marriage in the recovered areas, and issued a general order to the provincial governments, high courts, and senior military officers in the provinces and regions suppressing bandits in Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, Fujian, and Sichuan to comply. The order states: "Upon investigation, in the provinces within the bandit areas, in places occupied by the bandits, all rites, customs, and laws have been completely destroyed, and the relations between men and women are especially chaotic. They advocated the heresy of communal wives and lived a life of bestiality, so there is no such thing as a marriage system. Now that the army is advancing and suppressing the bandits, and the bandit areas are gradually being cleared, marital disputes will inevitably arise. However, the matters are complex and cannot be handled fairly solely based on ordinary laws. It is necessary to adapt to these special circumstances and formulate separate relief measures in order to maintain ethics and correct customs. Therefore, special measures for handling marriage in the recovered bandit areas are formulated, promulgated and implemented. In addition to separate orders, the handling measures are hereby issued, ordering the 'Provincial Government, High Court, and General Headquarters to comply accordingly, and to instruct their subordinates to be informed accordingly.' This order."

Measures for Handling Marriage in Recovered Bandit Areas: Article 1: These measures shall apply to the resolution of marital relationships in the bandit areas after recovery. Article 2: In these measures, "marital relationship" refers to a man and a woman having the intention of permanent common life and cohabiting. "Bandit area" refers to an area that has been occupied by Red Bandits. Article 3: If one or both parties of a married couple have been taken away by the bandits or have fallen into the bandit area and remarried, it shall not be considered bigamy or adultery. The validity of the marriage shall be as follows: 1. If both parties of the couple are willing to restore the original marriage after the recovery of the bandit area, the previous marriage shall be maintained and the subsequent marriage shall be dissolved, but it must be requested within one year. 2. If both parties of the couple are unwilling to restore the original marriage after the recovery of the bandit area, the previous marriage shall be deemed divorced. 3. If the husband or wife is willing to restore the original marriage after the recovery of the bandit area, but the other party is unwilling, the subsequent marriage shall be maintained, but the former husband may request compensation of up to 100 yuan from the latter husband. 4. In the case of the preceding paragraph, the former husband may demand compensation of up to 100 yuan from the latter husband, and the former wife may demand reasonable alimony from the original husband, but this shall not apply if the former wife has remarried or has been remarried. Article 4: Those who have been married more than twice in the bandit area may not request the restoration of intermediate marriages or compensation. Article 5: If one of the married couple does not return or there is no news for more than one year after the recovery of the bandit area without a legitimate reason, the other party may remarry. Article 6: Child support shall be borne by the father born in the marital relationship, but special agreements shall be followed if there are special agreements. Article 7: Matters not stipulated in these measures shall be governed by the Civil Code and its implementation law. Article 8: These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

After the Recovery of Hengfeng, Jiangxi, the Local Area Gradually Returns to its Former Appearance

Wuyuan Correspondence: Hengfeng is located in eastern Jiangxi, adjacent to Yiyang, Guixi, Qianshan, Shangrao, and other counties. Since it was occupied by the Fang Shao Communist bandits in the 17th year of the Republic of China as a base, it has been occupied for six years. This time, after being painfully suppressed and recovered by the National Army, the surviving people, who had been groaning under the poison of the sunken haze for a long time, were finally able to see the light of day again. According to a visitor from Hekou, the bandit nest in the county was broken by Commander Liang and completely recovered. The political training office of the division and the local authorities are currently preparing for post-disaster relief and striving to appease the people. The people in the bandit area and the refugees who fled to neighboring counties have returned one after another. However, the county area, which has been devastated for a long time, has destroyed farms and no houses remain. The victims are exposed to the wind and eat in the open air, and the situation is extremely tragic. The garrison has ordered the battalions and companies to build dozens of houses as a place for the returning people to live in. Now, the houses in the county seat are connected to each other, and the city is gradually returning to its former appearance. The market is thriving, and due to the increasing number of returning people, department stores and restaurants have reopened one after another. Postal and transportation services have also been restored. The 50-li highway from Hekou Dawangdu to the county seat has been completed by the Zhao and Wang Lv regiments. The highway from Shangrao to Hengcheng will also be open to traffic within the next few days. (19th)

T.V. Soong's Report on His Inspection of the Northwest

The National Economic Council held its ninth standing committee meeting on the morning of the 22nd. Committee member T.V. Soong reported on his inspection of the Northwest. The original text is as follows:

"The main purpose of my trip to the Northwest was to inspect the various construction projects undertaken by the Council in the Northwest. Today, I will first give a summary oral report for discussion. As for my overall impressions of the Northwest inspection, I will submit a detailed written report later.

(1) Water Conservancy: The Council's Focus. The Northwest has suffered from droughts and famines for many years, so we emphasize water conservancy construction. In Shaanxi, the Jinghui and Luohui canals in the cotton-producing areas are particularly important. Therefore, we are actively planning and rushing to build these two canals. The Jinghui Canal was originally a joint project between the China International Famine Relief Commission and the provincial government, costing 1.4 million yuan. In the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), it irrigated over 3,000 hectares of land. It urgently needs improvement to achieve its full potential. Therefore, it is proposed that the Council provide 250,000 yuan as a revolving fund for repairs and improvements. It is expected to be completed this winter and can irrigate over 5,000 hectares of land.

Regarding the Jinghui Canal, after my inspection, I have the following opinions: (1) The canal was built hastily, focusing on work relief. Therefore, all engineering plans were not well-developed, especially the management methods were poor, and the use of water from small branch canals was left to the farmers' discretion, resulting in water wastage and flooding of roads. (2) After the major disaster in the 19th year of the Republic (1930), the people's strength had not recovered, and the income from water levies was very small, resulting in a lack of funds for canal maintenance. In the future, management should be improved, and water levies should be collected conscientiously. The income can not only be used to maintain the canal but also to promote the construction of other water conservancy projects. I believe that this is not a local problem because the price of farmland has increased several times after the canal was built (from 5 yuan per mu before to over 30 yuan per mu now). It is fair to collect water levies for maintenance and to promote other water conservancy projects. If it can be handled properly and set a model, the obvious success will easily attract the attention of domestic and foreign merchants to invest in other water conservancy projects. The government's financial resources are limited. If we can encourage commercial investment, then the huge water conservancy problem in the Northwest will have a concrete solution. However, the Executive Yuan has an order that the collection of water levies per mu cannot exceed the canal's own repair costs. I believe that we should urgently request the Executive Yuan to amend it. The current regulations stipulate that the use of water levies, in addition to canal maintenance, can be used for the development of other water conservancy projects. This method is easy to implement because the people in the Northwest who benefit from water conservancy are willing to pay. Although the situation in Shaanxi is slightly different after the disaster, it can be easily handled with two years of good harvests if the fees are kept light. The Luohui Canal plan was originally planned by the provincial government to divert water from the Luo River for irrigation. Its irrigation area is also an important cotton-producing area. After irrigation, its productivity will be the same as the Jinghui area. It has now started construction and will be completed in two years, irrigating 5,000 hectares of land. The original budget was over 1.4 million yuan. The Council plans to invest 750,000 yuan this year as a revolving fund, and the provincial government will allocate 20,000 yuan per month until completion. The remaining tens of thousands of yuan will be allocated by the Council next year. The Council and the provincial government will jointly establish a water conservancy committee and a water conservancy engineering bureau to be responsible for handling the Jinghui and Luohui canal projects.

Wei River Diversion Plan. There are many water conservancy plans in Shaanxi Province, the most noteworthy is the Wei River Diversion Plan. (1) The Baoji Plan, proposed by German engineer Mr. Barke, roughly involves accumulating water in the Baoji Valley to generate electricity. The electricity will then be used to pump water from the Wei River to irrigate approximately nine million mu of highland fields on the north bank (according to other engineers, only two to three million mu). The remaining electricity will be supplied to various industries and the future Lanzhou-Xinjiang section of the Longhai Railway for train power. In my opinion, the cost is as high as 85 million yuan, which is not currently affordable. The supply of electricity still depends on the development of industry and railways. For the time being, we can only focus on irrigating fields. The cost of irrigation per mu is 17 yuan or even more than 30 yuan. Compared with the current water conservancy plans in the Northwest provinces, the average cost per mu is only about one to two yuan, which is not worthwhile. Therefore, the Barke plan only has value for reconsideration after the Lanzhou-Xinjiang Railway is open to traffic. (2) Committee Chairman Li Yizhi and others have another plan for diverting the Wei River, with a budget of 2 million yuan to irrigate over one million mu. This plan is worthy of study in terms of the country's current economic capacity.

Suiyuan Minsheng Canal. In the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the China International Famine Relief Commission and the provincial government jointly built the canal to relieve the drought. The total cost was over 860,000 yuan, and it was expected to irrigate about one million mu of land. Because the emphasis was on urgent relief at that time, no detailed surveys were conducted, resulting in the canal bed slope being too flat, the flow being slow and prone to siltation, and many places being washed away by floods. It is now completely abandoned. After the Council sent personnel to survey it, it was considered that it could be partially repaired. Detailed surveys are currently underway. Whether or not it can be started depends on the results of the survey. This canal project budget was resolved by the Council, allocating a revolving fund of 300,000 yuan. If the remedial measures are determined, it can irrigate six to seven thousand hectares of land.

The Council's water conservancy plan was originally limited to the Jinghui and Luohui canals. However, after inspecting the actual situation in Gansu this time, it was found that it has frequently encountered water and drought disasters, and the people are extremely poor. This is because the mountains are rugged, the climate is dry, and although there are many rivers in the territory, most of them cannot be used, and the ancient canals are also silted up and abandoned. It is recognized that it is necessary to operate them urgently. It has been found that near the Yellow River, once irrigated, the land can be turned into paddy fields. According to engineers, the work is easy and can irrigate over 1.8 million mu. After discussing with Chairman Zhu Shaoliang, if the Council can borrow 500,000 yuan, starting with easy work, it can irrigate 600,000 mu. The farmers are willing to repay one yuan per mu per year and recover this loan within one or two years as a revolving fund, which can be used to repair other canals in rotation. Within four or five years, Gansu Province can increase 2 million mu of fertile land to prevent drought and prepare for famine, with little cost and great success.

Ningxia Water Conservancy. Ningxia's Yellow River water conservancy has long been known as the best in the world. This time, the existing ancient canal projects were inspected and found to be relatively complete, unlike the complete destruction of Shaanxi and Gansu. The Qin Dam, Han Canal, and Tang Canal, projects that are more than a thousand years old, are still preserved. However, after Sun Dianying's war, the people suffered heavy losses. If the government uses relief methods to provide separate assistance, it is better to provide work relief. If 100,000 yuan is used to select important canal projects for repair, it can irrigate more than 100,000 mu of land and can also use the engineering corps of the 15th Army. Completion will be faster and the efficiency will be greater.

This time in Ningxia, the precision of the ancient water conservancy system and the economy of water utilization were amazing and admirable. Therefore, it is speculated that the ancient Qin and Long areas, which were known as rich areas, must have had water conservancy systems equal to Ningxia. The poverty today is due to wars in the past, disregarding the people's livelihood, leading to the abandonment of water conservancy, which has resulted in years of drought and famine. Therefore, it is felt that the most important thing for the country to build the Northwest in the future is security and water conservancy.

Qinghai. Qinghai's water and drought disasters are less than those in Shaanxi and Gansu. There are ancient canals that still exist and can be used occasionally. The province has a small population, mostly nomadic, and water conservancy is not urgently needed.

(2) Roads. In recent years, the northern provinces have built many roads, especially Director Yang Hucheng, Military Commander Ma Bufang, and Chairman Ma Hongkui have worked hard. The Council currently selects and repairs two main trunk roads based on important political and economic relations: 1. The Lanzhou-Xinjiang Line, and 2. The Xi'an-Hanzhong Line. The Lanzhou-Xinjiang Road was originally built by the International Famine Relief Commission with work relief. Later, the Council subsidized 200,000 yuan, and the road was roughly shaped. Due to lack of funds, the work was stopped. Many of the bridges and culverts that have been built have collapsed, and the slope must be reduced further. Before the Lanzhou-Xinjiang Railway is completed, this road is an important trunk road for transportation between the Northwest and the coastal provinces and international transportation between Europe and Asia. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek attaches great importance to this line and has repeatedly sent telegrams urging the work to be carried out in sections. It is planned to complete it with 800,000 yuan. The important projects are as follows: (1) Reduce the slope; (2) The bridge foundation has a load-bearing capacity of 10 tons, and the bridge deck has a load-bearing capacity of 7.5 tons, all based on freight trucks; (3) The geology of the Northwest is mostly viscous red mud. When it rains heavily, the mud is difficult to travel on and cannot be used for transportation. After sunny days, the driving is easy to damage. The fundamental remedy is to pave the entire road with stone. However, except for the Liupan Mountain, there is almost no stone available in the Gansu section. Transporting stone to repair the entire road requires at least 5 million yuan. Currently, we have to choose the most easily damaged sections of the road to barely pave with stone and select five important sections along the road to prepare five or six grader trucks. This type of truck is used on the Zhongshan-Macau Highway in China and has good experience. It is very fast and economical to repair roads after heavy rain. It can repair dozens of miles per day. With this equipment, it is estimated that on average, there will only be one or twenty days a year when it cannot be used for transportation. Under normal circumstances, it takes three days to get from Xi'an to Lanzhou and two and a half days to get from Lanzhou to Xi'an. This will greatly increase the convenience of transportation in the Northwest.

The main route for transporting goods from the Northwest is along the Yellow River through Qinghai, Gansu, Ningxia, and Suiyuan to Baotou, connecting with the Ping-Sui Railway. This is the most convenient route for freight transportation. However, the Yellow River can only transport goods downstream, and it can only be used for a few months of the year. Therefore, it is urgent to organize the Lanzhou-Xinjiang transportation line. The Northwest provinces are limited by financial resources and specialized talents, and they are also limited by provincial boundaries. Public buses are not easy to operate. The Council, under the order of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and at the request of the Shaanxi and Gansu provincial governments, plans to operate Lanzhou-Xinjiang bus transportation with 400,000 yuan. The purpose is to connect the transportation of important goods from Qinghai and Lanzhou to the Longhai Line and operate according to train schedules to facilitate merchants and travelers.

The Xi'an-Hanzhong Road. The Xi'an-Hanzhong Highway is an important line for economic and national defense. There is an incomplete motor road from Xi'an to Baoji. It is now planned to use this section to connect the main road from Baoji to Hanzhong. The preliminary survey has been completed, and two teams of detailed survey personnel have been sent to determine the route and construction methods within a limited time and to start construction as soon as possible. This road is planned to allocate 350,000 yuan this year. The Council selects these two tasks with its existing strength and focuses on operating them. The assistance of 8,000 to 9,000 military engineers dispatched by Chairman Zhu of Gansu and Director Yang of Shaanxi has greatly benefited the progress of the two roads.

(3) Health. The Northwest is more backward than other provinces in terms of health. In addition to basic health treatment institutions in major cities, there is no equipment in other parts of the province, and the people hardly know what health is. The Council plans to set up health experimental centers in Xi'an, Lanzhou, Xining, and Ningxia, and to set up branches in important cities to lead the improvement and expansion of existing public health treatment institutions in the provinces. For example, the recurrent plague in northern Shaanxi urgently needs to establish a health experimental center for prevention. The goal is to establish a health foundation for the tens of millions of people in the Northwest and to cultivate a strong nation.

Modern medical skills in the Northwest provinces are not well-developed. There are two reasons: (1) The area is poor, and medical talents from other provinces are unwilling to go west to serve; (2) Few children in the Northwest have the opportunity to study medicine in universities in other provinces, and a few people who can afford to study abroad are addicted to the comfort of life in the southeast or abroad and are unwilling to return to their hometowns to serve. Therefore, for the fundamental plan, after discussing with all parties, if the Shanghai Tongji Medical and Engineering Departments can be moved to Xi'an, children in the Northwest can study locally and not be contaminated by the luxury of other provinces. This can establish the foundation of medicine in the Northwest and cultivate the necessary construction talents in engineering. The government already has a large amount of subsidy for Tongji School every month. If it is moved to Xi'an, only the cost of building houses is required. The school is located in Shanghai, where schools are lined up. Its existence has little to do with it. If it can be moved to Xi'an, its benefits to the people of the Northwest are not insignificant.

Veterinary Medicine and Livestock Improvement. Animal husbandry is a major industry in the Northwest, but veterinary institutions can be said to have no equipment. Although there are no accurate statistics on the losses from animal epidemics every year, it is estimated that the loss in the death of cattle and sheep must be more than 10 million yuan. Therefore, the fundamental problem of animal husbandry is prevention. The Council plans to add veterinary experimental specialty courses to the above-mentioned public health institutions in the Northwest provinces and establish a serum manufacturing plant in Lanzhou. However, there are only five or six veterinary experts in the country. In addition to planning to hire domestic experts, it is also planned to hire four or five British and French experts with experience in Africa, Annam, and India to take charge of veterinary affairs in Gansu and Qinghai provinces. It is also planned to establish a veterinary school in Lanzhou, select outstanding soldiers from the army and local children, and strive to popularize it among the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui people. Experts from China and abroad will be professors to make veterinary knowledge and skills universal in the border provinces. The Council's livestock budget was originally set at 400,000 yuan, but after this inspection, it was believed that the initial foundation of animal husbandry should start with prevention. In the next few years, veterinary medicine will be the main focus, and livestock improvement will be the secondary focus. After discussing with experts, in order to concentrate efforts and facilitate progress, it is planned to merge the Northwest health and veterinary expenses. The original livestock 400,000 yuan, 100,000 yuan was transferred to water conservancy to increase funding, and 300,000 yuan was used for veterinary and livestock improvement expenses. Therefore, the Northwest health and veterinary original budget of 300,000 yuan, the public health, veterinary and livestock improvement will be merged, and the cost is about 600,000 yuan.

(4) Rural Construction. The rural areas of the Northwest provinces are declining and impoverished and urgently need relief. The Council's financial resources are limited, and we can only start with Shaanxi first. Because Shaanxi is an important cotton-producing area, it is especially important to prohibit the planting of opium poppies and switch to planting cotton to offset the income. The Cotton Industry Control Committee of the Council has set up a branch in Shaanxi to strive for improvement. Cooperation in production, transportation, sales, and credit needs to be expanded. The Jing River area uses the Jinghui Canal for irrigation to plant cotton fields. The Shanghai China Communications and other banks and public groups have been promoting cooperation in this area. However, the wheat fields outside the canal, which account for nine-tenths of the province, are not taken care of. After consultation with the provincial government, it is planned that the Council will allocate 200,000 yuan, and the provincial government plans to raise 500,000 yuan in installments. This will be used as a fund, either to release loans or to be used as a guarantee for bank loans. Banks can rely on this to increase the limit for releasing loans, and wheat farmers will benefit greatly. Although the Council spends a small amount of money, if commercial banks can release several times the amount of money because of this guarantee, the result will be more effective than the Council's direct release of loans.

The above sections are the feelings about the work of the Council after this inspection. The Northwest construction fee for this year, the conference originally stipulated in the outline in March. It is now proposed to revise the distribution within the possible scope as left:

Water Conservancy

Jinghui Canal Improvement Expenses 250,000 yuan

Luohui Canal Construction Expenses 750,000 yuan

Minsheng Canal Improvement Expenses 300,000 yuan

Gansu Canals Construction Expenses 500,000 yuan

Ningxia Canals Construction Expenses 200,000 yuan

Roads

Lanzhou-Xinjiang Road 800,000 yuan

Xi'an-Hanzhong Road 350,000 yuan

Shaanxi-Gansu Transportation Agency 400,000 yuan

Public Health Veterinary Medicine and Livestock Improvement 600,000 yuan

Rural Cooperative 200,000 yuan

Total 4,350,000 yuan

The above proposed amended distribution amount is for reference only. Whether it is appropriate is still subject to correction. (22nd)

Legislative Yuan Passes Savings Bank Law (Continued) Lottery Savings Should Be Strictly Prohibited Mr. Ma Yinchu Issues Statement

Ma Yinchu Talks about Prohibiting Lottery Savings. Ma Yinchu issued the following statement after the Legislative Yuan passed the Savings Bank Law: "When the Savings Bank Bill passed by the General Assembly today was submitted for discussion by President Sun, it can be said that it was unanimously passed by the entire audience and it was believed that it should be implemented quickly. Therefore, it was immediately submitted to the National Government for order and promulgation. It is expected to be implemented from July, because the original law stipulates that it will be implemented on the date of promulgation. As for cracking down on Wan Guozhongxi and other savings associations without hesitation, there will be no loss to the interests of depositors. Detailed opinions on this section are in my reasons for prohibition. The government should strictly supervise the various guarantees of lottery savings. The Ministry of Finance must have detailed measures. In this way, the huge amount of funds leaking from the vested interests can be recovered, and the legitimate savings of each bank can be guaranteed. On the one hand, the country already has methods to encourage legitimate savings, then each bank can also have great development in the savings business."

Reasons for Prohibiting Prize Savings Societies

Mr. Ma also published reasons for prohibiting prize savings societies, stating: "Prize savings harm the national economy to a profound and significant extent, necessitating thorough elimination. I am now briefly outlining several points below, hoping that various legal entities and public opinion representatives will unanimously support and widely publicize them to achieve the goal of abolishment, which would be a great fortune for the party and the nation." (1) The number of induced people is alarming. According to the Wan Guo Savings Society, the current total savings amount is approximately 65 million yuan, with over 116,800 members per term. The so-called "full member" pays 12 yuan per month; those paying 6 yuan are called "main members," and those paying 3 yuan are called "quarter members." In total, the number of absorbed savers is no less than 300,000 to 400,000, which is a significant concern. (2) Unequal treatment between Chinese and foreign entities is unavoidable. I drafted the Savings Bank Law, summarizing and quoting the savings bank regulations and proposals drafted by various parties since the late Qing Dynasty, which can be found in volumes 1, pages 475 to 534, of my collected essays. While the content may vary, there is unanimous agreement among all parties to ban prize savings. The Savings Bank Law passed today stipulates a ban on prize savings. Because the law strictly regulates genuine savings businesses, such as holding directors and supervisors jointly and severally liable, it is evident that the regulations are stringent. However, if the prize savings societies run by Chinese and foreign merchants are not mentioned at all, it would be unfair and cause pangs of conscience. The society's funds have already reached 60 to 70 million yuan. When it accumulates to 60 to 70 million yuan in the future, enforcement of the ban will be more difficult than it is today. If we don't act now, it will be too late to regret. (3) Overflow of lease rights. According to my recent investigation, the Wan Guo Savings Society has purchased the following properties: Shanghai Public Concession Works Bureau bonds, Hankou French Concession Works Bureau bonds, Shanghai Works Bureau bonds, Beijing Grand Hotel debentures, Siam Hotel Company debentures, Shanghai Ye Guang Company debentures, (foreign-run) English and French Real Estate Company debentures, Shanghai Puyi Real Estate Company preferred shares, Shanghai French General Association debentures, Hankou Western Merchants General Association debentures, Hankou Racecourse General Association debentures, Hankou French General Association debentures, Shanghai Yangpin Lending Bank shares, Shanghai China Construction Real Estate Company shares, Shanghai British Hengye Real Estate Limited Company Class A shares, Shanghai British Hengye Real Estate Limited Company Class B shares, Shanghai Huamao Real Estate Company shares, Shanghai Yeguang Real Estate Company shares, Siam Cement Company shares, Shanghai French Tram and Electrical Company shares, Shanghai American Asiatic Underwriters seven-percent preferred shares, Shanghai American Asiatic Underwriters eight-percent preferred shares, etc. From this, it can be seen that the funds absorbed from Chinese people are entirely used by foreigners. The exact amount is temporarily not disclosed. Sun Yat-sen had high hopes for building a new China. Utilizing foreign capital was a way to quickly achieve construction goals, as demonstrated by industrial plans. Today, we are not only unable to utilize foreign capital, but our own national funds are being used by foreigners. Chinese people are utilizing foreign capital, which has turned into foreigners utilizing domestic capital. If we don't strictly prohibit this, we will be betraying Dr. Sun Yat-sen's spirit in heaven. (4) Contrary to the New Life Movement. The essence of the New Life Movement is to uphold propriety, justice, integrity, and a sense of shame, and to be honest and not deceitful. However, prize savings societies aim to extract the lifeblood of our people through clever means. Where is the propriety? Savings are called "prize savings," and all savers have the hope of winning a prize, creating a situation of fierce competition, no different from gambling. The savers are all our compatriots, which is equivalent to leading our compatriots into injustice. The ancients said, "Do not acquire wealth by improper means," which is the key to integrity. Prize savings societies intend to deceive people for money, showing no integrity. Calling it insatiable greed would be quite accurate. Knowing that it is a scam, they still shamelessly call it savings, with no sense of shame. All of this is unbearable for those who promote the New Life Movement. (5) Severe embezzlement. According to the Wan Guo Savings Society's saving method, it is 12 yuan per month. If this amount were used for zero-deposit lump-sum savings, calculated at a monthly interest rate of 8%, compounded, after 15 years, the principal and interest would be 4,831 yuan. However, when the savings society matures, it only repays a principal of 2,000 yuan. The difference between the two amounts is 2,831 yuan, of which about 1,200 yuan is used for prizes, and the remaining 1,600 yuan is completely embezzled by people within the savings society. If one person is like this, imagine what it is like for more than 100,000 households. It's shocking! Moreover, it is developing rapidly. If we don't seek relief immediately, we may face a situation where it becomes too big to fail in the future. The calculation method for prize savings principal and interest can be found on pages 231 to 248 of the second volume of my lecture collection, so I won't elaborate further. (6) Hinders genuine savings. Our country's national funds are very limited, and those available for savings are even more limited. Usage and distribution are more abundant in this area, and must be smaller in that. Therefore, with the development of prize savings, the funds for genuine savings will inevitably be affected. To encourage genuine savings, we must strictly prohibit prize savings. (7) Improper handling by the Ministry of Finance. The Ministry of Finance currently levies several types of taxes on prize savings societies: one is stamp tax, with a tax of 3 cents for those paying 3 yuan per month, 5 cents for those paying 6 yuan, 8 cents for those paying 9 yuan, and 10 cents for those paying 12 yuan and 15 yuan. The other is a special tax of 5 yuan per month for new savers, totaling 60 yuan per year, for a one-year limit. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance's annual income from prize savings societies is considerable, but everyone knows the harm of prize savings. The government should find ways to eliminate it to avoid the misuse of national funds, so as not to betray the trust of the people. Now, the government is taking advantage of gambling opportunities to collect formal donations and taxes, which is equivalent to encouraging people to gamble. How can this be shown to the people? Moreover, we are now abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, and the disadvantages of this kind of donation and tax are far above excessive levies. The Ministry of Finance should set an example, remove this kind of evil tax, and not cherish the small income while letting it spread endlessly. Minister Kong strongly supported the ban at the Industrial and Commercial Conference in 1919. Now that he holds great power, he will surely follow his original aspirations and take swift action. (8) The absurdity of the winning numbers. The members of the Wan Guo and Zhongfa savings societies are scattered throughout the country, and they don't know each other. The lottery takes place in Shanghai. There is no permanent supervisory body, nor is there a fixed person to supervise. Whether the drawn numbers match those reported is impossible to prove. Whether the winners actually exist is also unknown. (5) Losses from savers mortgaging loans. The repayment period for savings is 15 years later, and during these 15 years, savers must pay monthly. Given the weakness of our people's resources and the instability of their jobs, few savers can pay to the end. On the contrary, many quit midway. However, the amount repaid when quitting is far less than the principal already paid. For example, if someone pays the full amount for two years, the principal would have reached 288 yuan, not counting interest. When quitting, the principal repaid is only over 90 yuan. The loss of interest is another matter. Those who use savings certificates to mortgage loans also borrow little. The amount withheld is enough to continue paying membership fees for one or a few years. If the loan is not repaid, the savings society will calculate it at compound interest, inevitably turning the saver into a debtor. Is there still hope of recovering the savings already paid? Their means of deception and exploitation can be said to be all-encompassing. (10) The head office is not responsible for the branches. Today, Wan Guo and Zhongfa savings societies not only set up agencies in trading ports, but also widely establish branches in the interior, using various scams on ignorant men and women. Once the savings are in hand, managers abscond with the money, which is often heard. The head office is not responsible, leaving the savers with no way to appeal, which is extremely painful. The incidents that occurred in Wuzhou and other branches can serve as a warning. (11) The harm of foreign prize savings is far above foreign banks. We often say that foreign banks absorb Chinese funds for the use of foreigners, which greatly harms our country's financial economy. Compared to prize savings, it is like comparing a small witch to a great one. Bank deposits still have interest to be earned, and the funds are mostly used for import trade with China. They don't have agencies in our country's interior. Prize savings societies are the opposite in every way. Not only do they not give much interest on the funds, but they also use them for speculative ventures, widely establishing branches in various counties and towns. Even the small savings from the hard work of ignorant men and women are the object of exploitation, and the harm is even greater. How can it be compared with foreign banks? (12) National dereliction of duty. The intentions of the savings society are as mentioned above, and it is truly unspeakable. The depth of the people's blind faith in foreigners must be severely corrected. The people have more faith in businesses run by foreigners. They rush to deposit money in a certain bank run by foreigners, fearing that it won't be accepted, and they have nowhere to entrust their safety. A certain savings society run by foreigners, they deeply believe, will never deceive them. They resolutely purchase savings with the hope of winning a big prize in the unlikely event. Among them, there are also a few Chinese people who greedily seek small profits and vigorously solicit customers, all of whom have failed in their national duty. (13) Prohibiting prize savings will not hinder the implementation of the Savings Bank Law. This Savings Bank Law was formulated with reference to the opinions of the Ministry of Finance and the Shanghai Banking Association. Their important opinions were almost completely adopted, so this law can be implemented immediately after it is promulgated. Director Xu of the Ministry of Finance also advocated implementing it from July 1, and it must not be delayed due to the prohibition of prize savings. (14) Prohibiting prize savings is neither anti-foreign nor does it exclude any individual. I have always advocated prohibiting prize savings. In 1919, when I served as a consultant to the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, I wrote two articles on the harm of prize savings and its calculation methods (now published in the second volume of my lecture collection). At that time, the Chinese bank that ran prize savings had extensive dealings with the Xingye Bank, saying that colleagues should not squeeze each other out. Mr. Chai Kuichu, the chairman of the Xingye Bank, asked me to step back. I argued for my position, so today's ban on prize savings is not anti-foreign, nor is it against any individual. Anyone who runs prize savings, whether it is a bank or a savings society, whether it is a foreigner or a Chinese, is opposed. (15) Prohibiting prize savings can prevent inland funds from flowing out. The ultimate goal is to make funds flow back into the

land and no longer allow inland funds to flow out. (16) Prohibiting prize savings is not afraid of embezzlement and absconding. Some say that once prize savings are prohibited, the people running them may abscond with the money. This need not be worried about. The chairman and directors of the Zhongfa Savings Society are Chinese, and the Wan Guo Savings Society also has Chinese directors. Its properties, such as bonds and mortgages, are kept by HSBC and Banque de l'Indochine, which issue receipts for safekeeping, and they are verified by Chinese and Western directors, auditors, and British auditing specialists. Since there are Chinese directors involved, absconding seems unlikely. This is the first reason. Even if they abscond, it is still worthwhile. For example, regarding those who pay the full amount for two years and then quit, as mentioned in item nine, although they lose over 190 yuan, if the 12 yuan per month is deposited in a bank, the interest earned by the end of the fifteenth year will be greater than the loss, and the loss will be even greater if they continue to pay. This is the second reason. Moreover, of the 65 million yuan in savings of the Wan Guo Savings Society, 20 million has already been lent to savers, so it will not be completely lost. This is the third reason. The Wan Guo Savings Society lends money to various companies, and the directors and supervisors of various companies also have Chinese people involved. For example, the amount invested by the Wan Guo Savings Society in Chinese business companies is no less than 3 to 4 million, and the directors and supervisors of Chinese business companies have Chinese people involved, and they are very influential people. It is not easy to abscond. This is the fourth reason. Therefore, I am not afraid of them absconding. (End)

Northwest Inspection Record

Mongolians' Forehead-Touching Marriage and Sky Burial, Our Newspaper's Special Correspondent

— Geng Ya

At 8:00 AM on May 1st, I visited the Rulai Ji Ling Temple. The temple is about two or three li away from the lodging. The halls, towers, and platforms are all built of white mud, as white as chalk. It can be seen from more than ten li away. There are Mongolian yurts inside for lamas to store food. There are two large halls, east and west. The east hall enshrines Buddha statues such as the Tathagata, which are still solemn, and there are many valuable items on display. The west hall enshrines images of deities and monsters such as Garan, Ox-Head, and Horse-Face. In the middle is the so-called "Happy Buddha" (Mongolian name "Demu Queke"), which is a male Buddha with four faces, entering arms, raised eyebrows, and exposed teeth, holding a jade-faced goddess with disheveled hair, both naked in an intimate posture, covered with yellow silk below. The lama instructed to lift the silk to view it, but the lewdness of it must be more than obscene spring paintings. When I asked about the origin of the Buddha, the lama stared blankly and couldn't answer. Mr. Zhu, who was traveling with me, said, "This probably symbolizes the primordial chaos, the creation of things and people, just like the Eight Trigrams of Fu Xi, the principle of yin and yang, but the latter is more elegant in conception, while the former is particularly vulgar in form." If that's the case, sculpting and placing it in temples, where lamas face it morning and evening, is not appropriate.

The tour guide lama was named "Dongdun." At first, he suspected that we were outsiders and refused to open the door. He spoke through the window and answered with "Mo de gui" (meaning "I don't know"). Later, Mr. Zhu explained our intentions in detail, and he began to speak Chinese and asked, "Are you from the 'Southern Government'?" Then he opened the door to welcome us and said that he "became a lama at the age of nine, went to Beijing at the age of twenty-five, and has three brothers, all of whom are lamas except for the youngest son, who lives as a layman. The meat and food needed in the temple (Mongolian lamas don't abstain from meat) are supplied by the family. He recites scriptures once a day in the temple, called small recitation. On the first and fifteenth day of the lunar month and the birthdays of the Buddhas, it is called big recitation. There are many lamas for the big recitation, and the expenses are all paid by the temple. The bells and drums are loud and very lively." On his bed was a red lacquer wooden box. When opened, it contained fried rice, ghee, tea bricks, etc., and a small photo of the Panchen Lama. There were several plasterers, originally from Shaanxi, who came here to suffer (doing work is called suffering, which is a common saying in the grasslands). For more than ten years, they talked in detail about Mongolian customs. The lamas stood around listening quietly and corrected any mistakes. The details discussed are briefly recorded below.

Mongolians are brave and don't engage in farming. They specialize in nomadic life. Both men and women are good at riding. Men especially like to race. Up and down the valleys,

Page 10

they are as fast as the wind. If they get sick, they burn themselves on the right side and don't tell anyone. Their food consists of mutton and cheese, which they own. Fried rice and clothing are mostly exchanged for sheep. Near the border, their food and housing have gradually become Sinicized. On the lunar New Year's Day, the royal family and nobles live in non-Mongolian yurts and still use Mongolian Spring Festival couplets. Ordinary people go to the Zhaomiao Temple, kowtow to the lamas, and after returning to the yurt for tea, those who pray for blessings or seek recovery from illness go outside the temple and circle it more than ten times. When relatives and friends meet, few pay respects. On this day, giving fire to others is most taboo. Eating meat is more plentiful than usual. If the elders or lamas give a Hada (a kind of silk fabric) or a horse's head and sheep's tail, the recipient will regard it as the highest honor and auspiciousness. On the fifteenth day, they invite the Grand Lama to touch their foreheads. The lama uses a wooden pole to tie red cloth and strikes each forehead. If struck, they are happy; otherwise, they wait for a long time and don't leave. The lamas of each temple have a big recitation from the New Year's Day to the fifteenth day, and also in June. The Grand Lama is also called the Living Buddha, sits in the hall and chants scriptures. The other thirty-two lamas wear python robes and colorful clothes, and wear masks on their heads, disguised as heavenly kings, Bodhisattvas, Ox-Head and Horse-Face images, beating drums and cymbals, eating large trumpets, sometimes dancing in pairs, sometimes jumping together. There is a ghost, kneaded with ghee and flour, its color is reddish brown, placed in a triangular wooden plate, lined with a triangular silk painting of a heavenly king, the plate is placed on the ground, and all the deity images dressed by the lamas make a suppressing gesture towards him one by one, and then dismember him with a wooden sword, chanting sutras, drumming and gongs, sending them far outside the temple and returning. On this day, the officiating lamas collect a lot of donations from the people (This kind of "big chanting" ceremony is also held in the Lama Temple in Beiping every year on the 29th day of the second lunar month. Spectators fill the road and call it "beating ghosts" or "dancing ghosts."

When parents die, men and women cry, ask the lamas to choose the burial, place the corpse in the desert or hills, and chant sutras to bless the dead to ascend to heaven. The next day, or three days later, they go to see, if birds and beasts (mostly domestic dogs) eat it, it is auspicious; otherwise, they ask the lamas to pray again and move the corpse to another place, and it must be eaten by birds and beasts before it is finished. This is called "sky burial." If it is a Grand Lama or a wealthy family, the corpse is carried to a stove pit behind the mountain and burned, which is called "cremation." The children of the deceased untie their braids, wear their clothes inside out, and stop after a month. They also invite lamas to chant sutras on every anniversary, and some cry on New Year's Eve, but they don't go to the grave to worship.

Marriage is determined by matchmakers, by private agreement, or by horse racing to determine the choice. The marriage age is mostly seventeen or eighteen for men and fifteen or sixteen for women. The wedding gifts and dowry are not fixed. The wedding is mostly at sunset. The groom rides a horse to the bride's house, and the father-in-law welcomes him in, kneels to his parents-in-law, and presents gifts. The bride sits in another room with a cloth covering her face. The matchmaker leads the groom to untie the braids of the two, and they bathe in the same basin. Then the groom divides a cooked sheep's neck into two and eats it with the bride, and then goes to the father-in-law's banquet. After the banquet, he says goodbye and returns. The bride goes with him, both riding good horses. When they arrive, a fire is set up outside the yurt, and the couple dismount and worship it together, saying "worship the stove god." Then they worship the parents-in-law and elders, set up a banquet for the guests, and laugh and joke until dawn. The next night, another yurt is set up for them to live together for three days, and then they return to the bride's house. The groom stays for three days, and then they return together. After marriage, no matter internally or externally, the woman's responsibility is always greater than the man's. Men are mostly idle, and women are mostly diligent. This is probably a common phenomenon. Some cattle and sheep property is jointly operated, and some is managed separately. If the husband and wife disagree, they divorce by throwing soil.

At 2:00 PM, we started from the Rulai Ji Ling Temple. The weather suddenly became hot, and we opened our clothes to face the wind. Old artemisia had just sprouted new leaves, four or five points long, and Malan flowers were also in full bloom everywhere. After thirty li, we passed a hillside with overlapping yellow stone layers, shaped like autumn clouds. There was a well under the stone, more than ten zhang deep. Three li away from the well, we saw three or four rooms of Banshen, more than two hundred sheep and dozens of white horses. To the west of the road was a depression, a lake with a circumference of about twenty li. The sandy beach by the lake was as white as frost. At night, we passed a salt beach about eight li long. The surface layer was white and hard, and the inside was soft soil and thin mud. Several camels sank and couldn't get up. When whipped, they made a long cry, which was unbearable to hear. The camels carried three to four hundred catties and walked fifty to sixty li. How could they not be tired in the dark night on the mud beach? Salt is an essential element for human life, but no one collected it. Abandoning the goods on the ground was harmful, which was regrettable. Later, it took a lot of effort to reach the dry land, called Zao Shu, and stayed there. That day, we traveled seventy li. There was a deep well. The place was called Zao Shu, which must have trees, but it was barren, just like the previous few days, which was very disappointing.

Sichuan Bandits Plan to Flee to the Yangtze River Basin, Exhausting Food in Tongjiang, the Red Bandits Flee From Chengkou to Wanyuan

Hankou Correspondence: The military campaign against the bandits in Sichuan Province has been going on for more than a year and has not been completely resolved. The process can be divided into four periods: the first was the fall of more than ten counties in northern Sichuan, the heyday of the Red Bandits; the second was the inauguration of Liu Xiang and the general offensive by the National Army; the third was the recovery of Sui and Xuan, the period of the Red Bandits' defense; and the fourth was the counter-offensive by the Red Bandits, the period of attempting to flee. The decline of the bandit forces is already evident, but although the area occupied by the bandits has shrunk, they still have tens of thousands of people. Wanyuan and Tongjiang counties are still within their sphere of influence. The mountains are high and the city is steep, making it impossible to capture them suddenly. Recently, because Tongjiang has exhausted its food, they will decide to abandon it and concentrate their forces in Chengkou, Wanyuan to flee east to the Yangtze River Basin, or retreat north to Zhenba, waiting for an opportunity to flee. The bandits in front of Tongjiang have begun to move backward. The Xu and Fan divisions are preparing to follow up and pursue, so as to capture Tongjiang in one go. Tang also ordered strict prevention of the eastward flight. The left and right wings can meet within days. On the 19th and 21st, Tang reported to Hankou in detail on the progress of the campaign and the Red Bandits' plans, which are briefly recorded as follows: (1) Since this road launched a fierce attack on Wanyuan, although all departments have made progress, the mountains are dangerous and the attack is difficult. The bandits resisted stubbornly and launched repeated counter-attacks with a large force. The 9th and 11th were particularly fierce. Fortunately, our officers and soldiers calmly performed their duties, so they did not succeed. They are now strictly isolating and reorganizing on the new line, waiting for the general attack. However, according to investigations by various departments and confessions from prisoners and bandits, the main force of the 49th, 30th and other armies are now in the area. The entire 33rd Army is in the Dazhu River area. The 4th Army's 75th Regiment and the 9th Army's 73rd and 77th Regiments are in the Huangzhongbao and Lizia areas. The entire 12th Division and one division each from the 9th and 30th Armies are in the Houping, Daping, and Kongjiashan areas. The majority of the 30th Army, three to four thousand people, are in the Guanchangba, Shimahe, and Qiujialiang areas. They have been fleeing fiercely to Chengkou, Shuangkouhe, and Bataishan in recent days. According to reports, bandit leader Xu Xiangqian is now seriously ill, and the troops are commanded by Zhang Guotao. Zhang declared to the bandits in Wanyuan that Tongjiang had exhausted its food and would be abandoned immediately, and that it would flee east to Chengkou and Wanyuan, where salt and rice would be convenient. It was found that the elite bandits were concentrated on the right wing of this road and had been attacking Chengkou and Bataishan fiercely for days. Their intention to flee east is clear. In addition to ordering strict prevention, a special telegram was sent for your information. (2) Local businessmen and people who escaped from the bandit area yesterday reported that Xu bandit held a meeting the day before yesterday and decided on three measures: 1. Defend Tongjiang as appropriate; 2. If Tongjiang cannot be defended, retreat to Zhenma Ziyang and fight a decisive battle in the fall; 3. Concentrate on Chengkou and Wanyuan and take the opportunity to flee east to the Yangtze River to open up a new situation. According to reports from Division Commander Xu Yaoqing and Fan Shaozeng Ma Chen, the bandits on our front from Qin Jiahe, Zhenlongguan, Yankouhe Liuping, and Wumuchang retreated completely to Caobachang, Xindianzi, Machang, Shichang, and Tongjiang on the night of the 20th. It seems that the bandits have abandoned the first method and will adopt the second and third methods. In addition to ordering Division Xu to send troops to firmly occupy the Zhenlongguan Pass, to follow up and pursue the bandits, and to order Division Fan to occupy Tongjiang, the right wing departments were ordered to continue to advance. Special report, (22nd).

After Bandit Gao Jumped Off a Cliff and Died, His Wife Who Kidnapped and Sold People Was Captured, The Suppression of the Red Bandits in Northwest Jiangxi Is Imminent

Nanchang Correspondence, bandit leader Gao Yongsheng, was a pseudo-Central Committee member, had studied in Russia, and was a backbone of the Red Bandits. Last year, after the pseudo-Central Committee transferred bandit Kong Hechong to Ruijin for training, the remaining troops of bandit Kong were led by bandit Gao to wreak havoc in northwest Jiangxi, which was extremely cruel. His crimes were so great that he was captured by the National Army a few days ago. The bandit realized that he could not escape being publicly executed, so he pretended to defecate and tried to escape by jumping off a cliff. Then the bandit's body was discovered. After confirmation by the garrison and Commissioner Cao, the bandit had indeed jumped off a cliff and died. His head was cut off. The Red Bandits in Northwest Jiangxi, the giant culprit has been beheaded, and it will not be difficult to completely eliminate them in the near future. According to sources, Gao bandit's wife was also captured by the Second Column of the National Army in Pingxiang and has now been escorted to Pingxiang for interrogation. (June 22nd)

Three Provinces Headquarters Regulations: Measures for Recruiting Bandits to Surrender, Showing Lenience and Generosity to Accelerate Bandit Collapse

Hankou Correspondence: The Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, considering that the remnant bandits in the three provinces have been repeatedly and severely suppressed, and an internal collapse is already apparent, with only the forces of Xu Haidong, Wu Huanxian, and others, numbering two to three thousand, fleeing in eastern Hubei, surrounded by various armies, the time for complete pacification is not far off. However, as there are many awakened elements among those who followed the bandits, in order to achieve complete success by simultaneously carrying out suppression and appeasement, and combining both force and leniency, a broad path to self-renewal should be opened up. Therefore, five points of measures have been specifically stipulated and communicated to all bandit suppression armies for strict compliance. The original order is as follows: "Considering that the remnant bandits in the three provinces are increasingly impoverished, this headquarters has been ordered to supervise their suppression, and complete pacification is imminent. However, while suppressing bandits and quelling rebellion relies on military force, guiding the situation to our advantage is also extremely important. Although there are many extremely wicked individuals among the bandits, there must also be many who are subjugated by coercion and forced to act against their will. In particular, the masses in the bandit areas have suffered greatly from the oppression of the bandits, have no way to survive, and their suffering is truly pitiful. Now that the national army is encircling and suppressing them, a situation of mutual destruction is imminent. Even if they are fortunate enough to escape, prolonged blockade will inevitably lead to the same fate. At this time, there must be many awakened elements who intend to surrender and return. Recently, according to the commander of the Bandit Suppression Headquarters of the Henan, Hubei, and Anhui border region, stationed in Huaidian, a telegram from subordinate Brigade Commander Wang stated that Xu Yizong, the false chairman of the sixth township of the second district, Xu Yiqian, a member of the executive committee, bandit soldiers and bandit civilians Xu Die and others, have surrendered with weapons. According to the confession of the false chairman Xu Yizong, the township is located in the Guanyintang Huwan area. They have already understood the deceptive tricks of the bandits and feel that the bandit area is extremely difficult, plagued by poverty and disease, and unable to survive. Therefore, the masses, carrying guns, risked their lives to surrender. If they are granted self-renewal, they are willing to serve the national army to redeem their previous crimes. They also stated that many bandit soldiers and bandit civilians in the bandit area have now awakened, but because the bandit leaders spread propaganda that our side executes all prisoners and surrendering individuals, they are hesitant and dare not try. Furthermore, in Jiangxi, important figures from the bandit side, such as various political commissars, have recently awakened and returned with the people. These situations prove that the internal affairs of the bandit army have already shown signs of collapse. The impact of this is of great importance. In order to broadly open up a path to self-renewal for the awakened elements on the bandit side, and to accelerate the collapse of the bandit forces, the following points to be noted have been established: (1) All military, political, and training personnel should vigorously promote the national army's leniency and generosity towards self-renewing elements. Those who surrender will not only not be held accountable for their past actions but will also be rewarded according to regulations. The specific facts of the national army's previous leniency towards all self-renewing elements should be widely publicized. (2) During frontline operations, each army should make simple slogans and try to distribute them within the bandit army to persuade them to surrender. Furthermore, slogans to be shouted by soldiers should be formulated, such as 'The national army treats surrendering elements well,' 'Those who do not want to be bandits, come here,' 'Those who surrender with weapons will be heavily rewarded,' 'Only surrendering to the national army is survival.' When our army approaches the bandit army, soldiers should shout these slogans to the red bandit masses. (3) Each army should conduct strict investigations into the words, actions, and thoughts of the red bandits who voluntarily surrender to prevent the red bandits from taking advantage of the opportunity to carry out their conspiracy of agitation and incitement. However, during the investigation period, efforts should be made to ensure that the surrendering individuals do not experience significant mental or material suffering to avoid hindering the path to self-renewal. (4) Each army should, within the possible range, persuade captured or imprisoned red bandits to renew themselves. During interrogation, non-criminal torture should be avoided as much as possible. Instead, they should be informed of the political situation in China and the crimes of the red bandits, so that they can voluntarily express their sincerity to the national army. (5) All self-renewing elements, after investigation and training, and when they are truly sincere towards the national army, should be properly settled and given work according to their abilities, and they should not be left idle. All of the above points must be strictly observed in order to achieve the great effect of simultaneously suppressing and appeasing, establish the moral authority of combining both force and leniency, and ensure our military victory and the early completion of our efforts. The future of bandit suppression truly relies on this. In addition to separate orders, it is hereby ordered that you comply and immediately forward the instructions to your subordinates for unified compliance, and report the handling situation to be filed for future reference. This order is issued by Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek and Deputy Commander Zhang Xueliang." (21st)

Songjiang: Robbery of Pilgrims Solved, Principal Culprit Apprehended

Shen Xuetao, the owner of Dingchang Paper Store outside the East Gate of this county, along with companions Chen Guoxiang, Zhou Shengfa, and more than ten others, went to Mount Wutai on a pilgrimage. Unfortunately, they encountered a robbery in Dingzhou. As previously reported, his family member, Shen Zhipeng, received a letter from Gu Baoshan, the director of the Beiping Telegraph Bureau, detailing Shen's encounter with the robbery and the situation of the capture, stating briefly that Xuetao took a Pinghan train to Dingzhou on the morning of the 18th of last month and hired ten donkey carts. About ten miles into the journey, two robbers on bicycles chased them. One held a pistol, and the other held a bayonet. The Yang couple in the first cart escaped. Xuetao, sitting in the second cart, was stopped and searched by the robbers under the pretext of searching for contraband. The cash of more than two thousand yuan that the pilgrims had with them was all looted. Xuetao knelt down and begged for a small amount of travel expenses to return home. The robbers, seeing Xuetao holding onto their clothes and seeing that there were many pilgrims, feared resentment and shot Shen Xuetao in the lower breast, killing him on the spot. The robbers then fled. After the incident, Guanghui, the abbot of Pujisi Temple on Mount Wutai, and Gu Shi, a small shop owner from Shanghai, recovered the body to the town, bought a coffin, and held a memorial service at Pujisi Temple, ordering the monks of the entire mountain to chant scriptures to comfort the soul. Master Guanghui went to Tianjin to visit Chairman Yu Xuezhong and requested the arrest of the murderer. The principal culprit, Yang, and the accomplice, Li, have now been arrested and interrogated. They will be sent to the scene of the crime in Dingzhou for execution to deter bandits. It is said that Shen's coffin will be returned in mid-October.
