Sugar Market: Tax Reduction News Affects the Sugar Market

▲ Sales of Blue, Red, and White Sugar Halt Uniformly

Yesterday, the sugar market experienced frequent declines in customs gold, and rumors of a potential tax reduction on foreign sugar, which had been circulating for days, became increasingly rampant. As a result, sales of blue, red, and white sugar all came to a standstill. Sellers feared a dramatic change in market prices and mostly remained on the sidelines, rendering the public association's pricing efforts almost useless. The market calls yesterday were also extremely chaotic, with the highest bid at 20.5 yuan and the lowest at 20.3 yuan. There were also rumors of secret deals at lower prices, but these could not be confirmed. In short, everyone was confused by the talk of tax reductions. However, it is difficult to say whether the tax reduction will actually be implemented, and all parties are secretly exploring the situation. As for the domestic Chaoqing sugar, the inventory is indeed thin, and sales are still long. Even if the foreign sugar tax reduction is implemented, it will not have much impact, because the current market price is not high, and it is difficult for foreign sugar to be cheaper than domestic sugar even with a tax reduction. As for Hainan red sugar from Guangdong, because the sugar tax there has already been contracted, and there are plans to implement an agricultural tax increase on the 18th, most of the sugar in that area has been transferred to Hong Kong and loaded onto the Xinjiang ship, which arrived in Shanghai yesterday, totaling more than 4,000 bags.

Dried Goods: Orchid Seeds Show Signs of Crop Failure

▲ Old Goods Suddenly Rise in Price

According to a letter from Zhangzhou, the current state of new orchid flowers indicates a crop failure. The harvest this year may only be 10% of the usual yield. As a result, the market price of old goods has suddenly tightened. For top-quality all-yellow goods, Shanghai brokers are already willing to pay a high price of 50 yuan. Therefore, the merchants have wired the local area to ship the goods, and they may arrive soon.

Silk and Tea: Black Tea Prices Stable

Shenbao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Discussions

Amateur Consumer Cooperative

— Taoran

The world economic panic is deepening day by day. The weakness of general purchasing power and the increasing unemployment rate not only have not subsided, but have further expanded rapidly and extensively every day. Needless to say, we ordinary citizens are "bearing the brunt," especially we salary-earning class in the professional field, who are most likely to be drawn into the vortex of this economic panic crisis first.

We are now standing precariously on the tip of an economic panic volcano!

Therefore, we have no doubt that on the eve of this panic crisis descending upon us, we cannot afford to be ignorant. How should we prepare in advance to cope with the terrible crisis that is about to befall us?

So here, I offer an effective method to our comrades in the salary-earning class of the professional world:

In 1844, in Rochdale, England, a group of flannel factory workers jointly organized a consumer cooperative. Their business was: (1) to set up a cooperative store to supply the daily necessities of the members; (2) to build or purchase public dormitories to provide accommodation for the members; (3) to manufacture consumer goods for the members, accommodating unemployed members; (4) to rent or purchase land to provide unemployed members with cultivation; (5) to establish temperance societies to promote abstinence from alcohol.

Summarizing their business, we can see that it has at least the following benefits: (1) Because the profits from the cooperative store can still be distributed to the members according to their purchases, there is no waste in consumption, which can save expenses and increase the purchasing power of the members; (2) Because there are manufacturing and farming production businesses, unemployed and jobless members can temporarily avoid the panic in life caused by unemployment; (3) Having public dormitories can create close relationships between the families of the members and provide opportunities for cooperation and mutual assistance; (4) The rules on abstaining from smoking and drinking mean that people with bad habits and bad behavior cannot join the cooperative, which indirectly improves social morals and bad customs.

In fact, the effectiveness of consumer cooperatives does not stop at these points. In addition to improving human economic life and social systems, it can also train autonomy, increase organizational skills, support educational effectiveness, and develop cultural undertakings under collective action. Therefore, after the establishment of the Rochdale Consumer Cooperative, various places scrambled to imitate it and organized collectively. Up to now, the number of consumer cooperatives worldwide has exceeded 200,000, with more than 140 million members. This astonishingly high-speed development is unmatched by any social movement in the world. However, in our country, which is the most backward in accepting world trends, the cooperative movement has only had considerable development in rural areas, while in urban areas, it is silent and unheard of, and even if there is, it is only as rare as morning stars!

The tide of the world economic panic is already rolling like a flood under our feet. Our purchasing power is weakening day by day, and the panic of unemployment is constantly jumping around us. Our current position is exactly like that of the Rochdale workers in 1844. Our environment has the urgent need to organize consumer cooperatives. We really need to stand up immediately to organize amateur consumer cooperatives!

The business we can do at present is: (1) cooperative stores to supply our daily consumer goods to save expenses; (2) public dormitories to provide our accommodation, reducing many wastes and troubles in renting alone; (3) public entertainment venues and entertainment rooms to provide our amateur appropriate entertainment and recreation; (4) public libraries to provide our academic cultivation and enrich our own strength; (5) and various other public undertakings that we deem necessary to hold.

Comrades of the professional world who live on salaries: We should recognize the crisis we are facing, and we should stand up immediately to do some preparatory work. For society and for ourselves, we cannot delay any longer.

We should stand up immediately to organize amateur consumer cooperatives!

Life

(Fairy) (Cave)

— Ms. Ningna

Every time I pass by the XX Women and Children Relief Society, and occasionally catch a glimpse of several yellow and thin children through the narrow half-open door, my heart feels as if it is being pressed down by something heavy. It is the unspeakable human sympathy that evokes the sadness. This heavy sadness has been pressing on my heart for several years, and I have not forgotten it for a moment, especially when I see those little lives struggling in the same miserable fate. Maybe that day is coming soon! These large numbers of suffering orphans will jump out of the deathly terrifying circle and walk into the great "life road"! I hope so.

In my hometown, there is also an orphanage founded by several well-known philanthropists. In addition to accommodating orphans like other charitable organizations, it also opened up an orphanage park by taking advantage of the natural beauty. The park does not occupy a large area, but it is characterized by the abundance of flowers, especially chrysanthemums. Every autumn, there is always a chrysanthemum art fair lasting for several days, using different kinds of bright chrysanthemums to form various flower mountains, flower forests, and even flower stories. At the same time, wonderful performances are held in the chrysanthemum industry. Cultivating those flowers and plants and repairing the park are the work of the accommodated orphans. Usually, each person has to buy a ticket to visit there, and the price of the ticket is one dime (it is said that the money is used by the authorities to install equipment related to the health of the orphans), but if you want to see the "miracle" inside, you have to pay a special fee.

In the park, near the orphans' dormitories, there are two small hills facing each other in the east and west, with a dark cave at the bottom of each hill. This is the so-called "miracle." (And the park, or even the orphanage, is probably opened for this "miracle," I think.) Legend has it that they are "Royal Sealed Caves" left over from the Qin Shihuang era. Because many ancient bottles, ancient coins, ancient swords, and the like have been unearthed there, the two dark caves have been valued and treasured, and two iron gates have been artificially manufactured and sealed at the entrance of the cave. The inside has been constantly going down and the sloping earth slope has been replaced with stone slopes. Because they are relics left by a generation of heroes, everyone is eager to "see it for themselves" and scramble to look at the "miracle." The income of six copper coins per person is said to be considerable, but that was at the beginning. Later, as time went by, the "miracle" was forgotten, and the two caves became the nests of snakes. At some point, a rumor suddenly spread that a "Lingzhi grass" had grown in the eastern cave. Lingzhi grass is a fairy seed, and the cave has simply become a "Fairy Cave." Therefore, the weeds growing all over the way, tourists' footsteps are full again.

Regardless of the origin of the "fairy grass," the orphanage authorities' hard work for this exceptional business is evident. Next, let's look at the place's owner, the orphans' whole life:

The earth revolves around the sun eternally, and the work of the orphans there is the same from morning to night without stopping. As soon as it dawns, they climb down their small plank beds (the beds are made of wooden frames and divided into four layers, those who sleep on the second layer and above must use a ladder to climb up and down) and start their morning work, such as watering flowers and weeding. Breakfast is just thin millet porridge, limited to two bowls per person. In the morning, they are divided into classes like elementary school students. Lunch and dinner are the same coarse rice with side dishes, and the quantity is the same as breakfast. The entire afternoon is when they participate in production. Some weave rattan ware, some weave bamboo ware, some weave towels. Within a limited time, each child must complete a certain amount, otherwise, they will be beaten or starved. Even a six-year-old child does not have the good fortune to escape the strict rules. Therefore, the production is increasing day by day, and it is also easy to sell. Looking at the situation, the income from the goods is probably several times the orphans' consumption.

Most of the orphans are sent by relatives without parents, and the procedures for entering the hospital are very complicated. After finding a "solid" guarantor, you also have to find a letter of introduction from a powerful person before the child can enter. Some also have mothers, but the mothers are unable to support the children, so they entrust someone to send them in, but the procedures are more troublesome than the former, and sometimes they have to spend some money.

Page 20

Professional Self-Cultivation

Sibling Company

— Fu Lan

On the eve of the outbreak of the European War, a 53-year-old small tea merchant died in Seaford, England. His will entrusted the business to his daughter. At that time, Miss Eliza Baker was just a teenager, with no understanding of business or the ways of the world. Everyone expected this small business to close down for good. Who knew that she would shoulder this burden and struggle against the environment with her two younger brothers, who were still in school. Today, this small business has expanded into the well-known Baker Limited, with an annual turnover of about 10 million Chinese dollars. This is truly an inspiring story.

When these three siblings inherited their father's small business, they specialized in packaging tea, renting two cellars in a Methodist church. The place was dark, the air was foul, it was practically hell. Later, Miss Baker married Mr. Gaskin and abandoned the tea packaging business, switching to packaging dried green peas, which proved to be even more profitable. So she rented a better room and started her business. When the war ended, her two brothers joined her in her work.

A young woman and two students who had just left school were sitting in the office. Outsiders would never believe that they were the main figures controlling the entire business. Once, a customer came in and said to Mrs. Gaskin, "May I see anyone?" "Sure, you can see me," she said. "Yes, but I want to see someone who knows business," the customer earnestly requested.

Because of their young age, they did not look like important figures in the business, especially her younger brother, who was often mistaken for an office boy by outsiders. Therefore, they had to hire an older person to be their nominal manager. So they worked together, and the business grew day by day, until three years ago. From then on, they began to experiment with making canned green peas, with the three siblings working together. They first sent their manager to the scientist who invented the manufacturing method to study for three days. But in the end, no one told them how to use this new invention. They had to assemble a small model machine for making canned green peas, and the three siblings, together with their manager, discussed and experimented day and night, hoping to discover the secret of manufacturing. They had no expert guidance, and they did everything themselves.

So they accumulated a large sum of money and built a new factory. Their hard-earned savings were almost entirely invested in this uncertain new venture. If they failed, their fate would be sealed, so everyone worked even harder and more cautiously. In the first week they started manufacturing, orders from all over the place flew in like snowflakes, piling up on Mrs. Gaskin's desk, more than a foot high. The machines ran day and night to meet the enthusiastic needs of customers. The three siblings stood by the machines from morning till night, rarely having time to sleep. Batch after batch of their products were shipped out in bundles before they had time to cool down, to meet the needs of their customers.

Mrs. Gaskin went to the warehouse every day to inspect the green peas. She also often went to Lincolnshire to visit farmers, inspect the planting of green peas, manage the machines, supervise the printing, and take care of general affairs. She was practically doing the work of several people and never had a moment to spare.

They are now planning to build another new factory from next year to manufacture other canned fruits and vegetables, hoping to achieve an annual turnover of about 15 million Chinese dollars.

Everyone believes that the poor orphans are enjoying a very prosperous life, but who knows that this is just an illusion? The children are suffering inside, and the heavy manual labor is devouring their innocent and lively nature. There are no rosy, round cheeks to be found, only thin, yellow faces and scabby scalps. Sores are studded all over their frog-like, weak bodies. No one lets out a loud laugh, and no one dares to utter a lovely cry. And the teacher, who is like a prison guard, has never shown them a gentle expression. The lonely little souls are suffering in the 　 palace....

Once, a child was allowed by the teacher to meet his mother in the parlor. The mother looked at his bloodless face in amazement, and the child meekly accepted the unfamiliar caress. The mother began to cry sadly, not knowing what she was thinking, and the child reached out his small hand to tell his mother: The teacher had beaten him with a wooden stick in the morning. Coincidentally, their teacher walked past the door, immediately drove the mother away, severely beat the talkative child, and then locked him in a dark room to starve.

Mothers outside no longer laugh happily, and children inside no longer want to work miserably. When they see the wealthy children wearing new clothes and following their wealthy fathers, jumping and laughing in the park through the cracks in the bamboo fence on a beautiful day, what a powerful stimulus that is for them! 　　 Things finally happened. Two children, taking advantage of the teacher's carelessness, ran away from the mountain behind the courtyard, but were caught by the teacher not far away. It is said that the punishment was particularly severe that time. After being beaten violently, they were sent to the "Fairy Cave" for solitary confinement. The children were crying and shouting as they were thrown in. By the time they were dragged out, the children were silent. The youngest, who was only six years old, lost his suffering little life in the "Fairy Cave," and the nine-year-old had only one last breath left....

The earth revolves around the sun eternally, and the children suffer eternally in the orphanage. The orphanage, surrounded by the light of charity, exists eternally.

International Radio Station

Soviet Water Happiness Society

— Fusheng

The public organ for developing water transport and water rescue 丨Water Happiness Society (Osvod)丨has been reorganized from the former Water Relief Society. The latter was solely focused on water rescue and had a total of 48,000 members.

The Water Happiness Society was rebuilt and established in 1931. Its articles of association and detailed rules are completely different from those of the former Water Relief Society. Its goals have been newly revised; it connects itself with the rest of the country and strives for socialist construction in the same way. Its main work is to help the development of water transport, encourage the construction of small boats, and train sailors and drivers, etc.　　The achievements of the past two years of activities have shown that the goals it has adopted are correct. Now it has a total of 500,000 members, and most of them are very active members. Three thousand local branches have been established in the past two years. Most of these branches are located in working-class communities near water areas.

In a revolutionary anniversary festival in 1932, the association held a mass parade. There were 400 kinds of achievement reports in line with the association's activity goals, and the lively water sports held at the same time attracted 1.5 million 　spectators.

In the struggle for ship repair, the association mobilized 250 teams to participate, repairing a total of 175 giant ships. In order to save material waste and increase the speed of ship repair, a work to improve the education and technical level of members has been carried out.

During the spring and summer seasons suitable for navigation, the association made the greatest effort to utilize all the ships to their full effect. The ships belonging to the association carried a total of 2.5 million passengers during that period, including collective farmers carrying goods to the city.

Printed propaganda materials were also used extensively. In 1932, it printed 25 kinds of popular pamphlets discussing its various activities. It also printed 18 kinds of art advertisements, each in large quantities, instructing the public on how to save a person drowning in the water, how to save fuel, how to avoid grounding and hitting reefs, etc.

At docks and shipyards, the association spends a total of 65 million rubles each year to build small wooden boats and various types of ships (such as speedboats, steamships, lifeboats, ice-skating boats, etc.), and another 2 million rubles to equip various appliances on the ships. About 3,000 graduates have graduated from the crash courses organized by the association. After passing theoretical and practical work, they have been employed as regular water transport sailors and boatmen.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

Introducing "Vocational Life" Bi-Monthly Magazine

— Ye Feng

I accidentally bought the inaugural issue of the "Vocational Life" bi-monthly magazine at a newsstand. After reading it, it aroused my excited sympathy and resonance. Here I should sincerely introduce it to our shop assistants.

First of all, we must understand that this publication is not a garden for literati and elegant people to show off their style, nor is it a tool for vocational educators to teach and deceive us. It is purely painstakingly founded by several young people in the vocational world, so its appearance is not an accidental trick, as stated in the inaugural message: "From the name of this publication, you can realize that it is for people in the vocational world... In the current tense situation, the bankruptcy of the countryside, the sharpness of imperialist aggression, and the economic panic have led to massive unemployment of shop assistants, and those who are employed are also feeling the pressure of unemployment panic at all times... Under the oppression of material things, in order to solve our urgent and serious problems, in order to uncover the darkness of the vocational world and expose the tragic lives of vocational youth, to awaken the self-awareness and progress of the entire lower-level shop assistant masses..." Undoubtedly, it is a child of the times. It was produced in the current severe era. Shop assistants have begun to issue the first cry in history. What kind of encouragement and comfort is this cry to the wounded hearts of our shop assistant masses?

In order to complete its declared mission, to match the painful tone of our lives, the development of the content is realistic, fully showing a resolute and strong warrior's face. There is no frivolous laughter, no boring talk, no mysterious academic theories, no hypocritical embellishment of benevolence, righteousness, and morality, but the truth of explaining the sins of the present society, revealing the bloodstains and tears of our lives, and reflecting the ferocious face of the vocational world. For example, in the vocational communication column "Our Lives," in this communication, a

The fragile and tragic heart of a young apprentice in a glass factory pours out his wailing for his living environment and sheds tears of sympathy for a companion who suffers innocently. At their young age, they lost their mother's love due to economic oppression and suffered the punishment of life under the iron whip of the economy. No wonder he asked suspiciously: "Did we bring sin from our mother's womb?" The communication "In the Silk Factory" objectively narrates the oppression and destruction of female workers by foremen, writing out the tragic facts that the author himself witnessed. Look! He lamented so much: "Every day, every day, I see countless ignorant female workers being trampled on and despised by those gentlemen who call themselves the management class; every day, every day, I see pure and innocent girls rushing out of the dilapidated countryside and throwing themselves into this machine that produces profits and exploits the surplus value of laborers, and one by one they are buried in the tomb; every day, every day, I also see boxes and boxes of silk being exported in exchange for thousands of dollars; every bright silk is stained with the blood, tears, and sweat of the laborers, but the people who wear silk feel very comfortable and relaxed." This scene aroused his infinite indignation and aimless hesitation. He deeply felt disappointed with his occupation, and a young man with ambition shed tears in this iron prison of life. "The Crippled Body" in the literary and artistic creation column (not yet completed in this issue) realistically describes a bank clerk who develops lung disease due to overwork. When he can no longer devote himself to bank affairs, the bank authorities kick him out like a leather ball. I am sorry that I do not have time to introduce the other works one by one.

Based on my observations, I believe that this is a good reading material for our shop assistant masses. As long as we are a shop assistant, everyone admits that it is our common tongue and mouth, conveying our common pent-up anger and resentment. It is the pioneer of our thoughts, leading us to judge truth and deception. It is the garden of our knowledge, cultivating our knowledge to move forward. Therefore, this publication is worth introducing here.

The magazine is priced at two cents per issue and four dimes per year. It is sold in major bookstores and newsstands. I am attaching this introduction.

The two rivers of Gamma), has now gradually recovered; the ships destroyed in those years have now been rebuilt. The construction in this area has grown significantly since 1929. The number of lifeboats has increased from 371 in 1929 to 961 in 1933, most of which are newly built. The number of lifesaving equipment has increased from 1,141 in 1929 to 2,249 in 1933. In 1932, 93 percent of the total number of people who encountered danger in the water were rescued.

With a basic understanding of lifesaving work, the association has formulated a budget to solicit an investment of 40 million rubles for more effective development in the future, which will be used to build and repair various lifesaving water equipment.

The purpose of this association is to realize the following slogan: "Never have a water casualty!" All lifesaving work is based on the concept of realizing this goal.

Commentary

Reasons for the Decline in Teachers' Status

— Zai Lian

The decline in teachers' status in society is an undeniable fact. We don't need to quote classics and allusions. Just mentioning a few of the nicknames for teachers is enough to prove it. Such as "Monkey King" and "Schoolteacher" all contain derogatory meanings. So why are teachers despised? The reasons are: First, because of the teachers' miserable life. Nowadays, people generally measure other people's abilities based on the amount of money they earn. Teachers' work is heavy, and teachers' remuneration is very low. Some monthly incomes are less than ten yuan, and a position with twenty to thirty yuan is considered rare. At most, it cannot exceed forty yuan. In today's rising cost of living, it is often felt that "eight bottles have only seven caps" to control this small amount. If you can afford rice, you don't have money to buy firewood. Teachers have no choice but to save money and use it sparingly. If you encounter years of salary cuts and arrears, there is no second way to go except to tighten your belts and wait for death to come.

The second is that there are no strict restrictions on teacher qualifications. "People's trouble is that they like to be teachers." The importance of the responsibility of being a teacher can be imagined. But even so, there are still many people who do not understand what education is, and who teach and gesticulate in the classroom with arrogance, so that the achievements of education are not worth hearing. There are also profit-seeking merchants who have suffered economic changes and lost their jobs, and have also entered the education sector. Regardless of Zhang San and Li Si, as long as they have a little knowledge, they can enter the education sector, which makes the education sector more complex. A certain celebrity said that teachers are as numerous as dog hair, which is also true. However, it is too harsh to compare teachers who are engaged in sacred careers to dog hair.

The third is that teachers' positions are not guaranteed. The life of a teacher can be said to be a short-lived life. The term of validity of the contracts of some schools is one semester, and that of others is one academic year. When the contract expires, those who are confident that they can renew can temporarily feel at ease. The standard for renewal naturally depends on the principal's feelings for you, and there is no so-called guarantee of a "service regulations" at all. If there is no hope of renewal, then you have to attack other schools again. If the attack fails, there will be the threat of unemployment. The unemployment of the

Small Monograph

Agricultural Laborers in Spain

— Naifu

Recent foreign dispatches report that 150,000 tenant farmers in Spain have launched a massive strike. "Fighting with local militias is occurring everywhere, resulting in numerous deaths and injuries. They would rather let the abundant harvest, unseen in fifty years, rot in the fields than accept the employers' demands. Their strike declaration states: 'We have endured hunger and starvation for two years. Even further deprivation is commonplace.'" (See Shen Bao, June 10th). What a heroic and poignant cry!

We know that Spain is an agricultural country. Of its 20 million people, about 7.5 million are employed, and those engaged in agriculture account for more than 50% of the total employed population. However, the concentration of land is unparalleled in the world. 67% of all cultivated land belongs to 2% of the population, who are large landowners owning more than 100 hectares. Conversely, 76.5% of landowners with less than 5 hectares (1 million people) own only 7.4% of the total cultivated land. This situation can be seen in the table below.

Category Number Percentage Average Land Holding per Person (Hectares) Total Holdings Percentage

Large Landowners 50,000 1 464.0 25,200,000 51.5

Rich Farmers 700,000 14 22.6 15,800,000 25.2

Middle Farmers 1,000,000 20 5.0 5,000,000 11.1

Poor Farmers 1,250,000 25 0.4 1,000,000 2.2

Agricultural Laborers 2,000,000 40 丨丨 丨丨 0.0

Total 5,000,000 100 丨丨 45,000,000 100.0

Agricultural relations in Spain are characterized by the prevalence of tenant farming, with feudal exploitation still persisting. Most of the two million agricultural laborers have no land at all and rely entirely on daily wages to survive. In a sense, agricultural laborers are an intermediate layer between farmers and the proletariat, because small farmers are increasingly becoming agricultural laborers due to heavy exploitation, while agricultural laborers themselves constantly wander between rural and urban areas in search of work.

Since the World War, Spain has been permanently mired in an agricultural crisis, and peasant revolutions and unrest are almost constantly heard. The peasant movement of 1919 reached its climax, with the Spanish government reporting as many as 160 tenant farmer strikes that year. Needless to say, these strikes were mainly led by agricultural laborers. Moreover, each strike is united with the movement of industrial laborers, and there are often mutual support strikes. Especially since 1929, the raging tide of the global economic crisis has intensified Spain's agricultural crisis, which has plunged Spanish farmers, especially agricultural laborers, into a more miserable situation, forcing them to launch a vigorous liberation struggle with a resolve to die.

Unemployment among agricultural laborers is a chronic phenomenon, and wage levels are extremely low. Moreover, the period of employment for agricultural laborers per year is very limited, generally limited to planting and seasonal work. This reflects the temporal characteristics of the Spanish agricultural movement. The average wage for agricultural laborers in Andalusia in 1931 was 3 to 4 pesetas. The average number of working days for agricultural laborers in that region is only 200 to 250 days per year, so the total annual income is only 700 to 900 pesetas. An income of 1,000 pesetas is extremely rare. Therefore, based on 365 days, the average daily wage is only about 2 to 2.5 pesetas. This is not even enough to cover the living expenses of a single bachelor, let alone supporting parents and raising a wife and children.

The working hours of agricultural laborers are very long, and working extended hours, up to 12-14 hours, is extremely common. As for the abuse of child labor and female labor, it goes without saying.

The agricultural crisis has worsened the state of agricultural laborers. First, unemployment has increased and the population has decreased. Second, nominal prices have risen, especially the nominal prices of necessities, which directly affect agricultural laborers because they are not sellers of agricultural products but only buyers. In the summer and autumn of 1931, agricultural laborers went on strike to force large landowners to raise nominal wages, but the large landowners further increased the nominal prices of necessities. As a result, the real wages of laborers actually decreased.

However, the rise in nominal prices of agricultural products is not only unfavorable to agricultural laborers but also of no benefit to poor and middle farmers. Due to the particularity of Spanish farmers' crops (grapes being the main agricultural product), they generally have to sell their crops before they are ripe to repay debts, pay taxes, and purchase necessities for agricultural management. They are fundamentally in an unfavorable position in terms of sales. Moreover, the plight of poor and middle farmers is exacerbated by tenant farming relationships. Large landowners often act arbitrarily and abuse their power. Whenever the lease term expires, they always arbitrarily increase the deposit and raise the rent, completely disregarding the value added by tenant farmers' labor on the cultivated land.

Regarding the farmers' poverty and destitution, we do not have statistical reports at hand, so let us cite some real-life examples.

Let us look at the situation in the two counties of Lorca and Águilas in the province of Murcia. Droughts plague them every year, and no crops can grow without artificial irrigation. However, the irrigation system in these counties has completely collapsed. This has forced the agriculture of this province (mainly grape cultivation) to decline, especially in the aforementioned two counties. In seven years, the agricultural population of Lorca County has decreased from 80,000 to 50,000. The agricultural population of Águilas County has decreased by 90%. Wine production in the two counties has decreased from 53,000 hectoliters in 1918 to 2,000 hectoliters in 1932. The total value of agricultural products has decreased from 35,000 pesetas to 23,000 pesetas. Year after year, tens of thousands of farmers who are uneasy about their livelihoods flow into cities, demanding relief, work, and bread. Examples like this are common throughout Spain.

no one esteems the teacher.

Fourth, contradictory phenomena in society cause teachers to completely lose their faith. Children hear great principles from teachers, but when they look at the objective environment in society, many situations are completely contrary to what the teachers say. Children's faith in teachers cannot help but waver at first, and eventually they become skeptical. For example, superstition does not help to save the country. This is something that children often hear from their teachers, and they certainly believe it to be true. But the reality that falls before their eyes is that some people are advocating chanting scriptures in the region, and teachers are even urging them to participate in this movement. Children's young minds cannot help but feel disgusted by the contradiction between the teachers' words and deeds. As for the fact that teachers are afraid of breaking their rice bowls and have to cater to the psychology of their superiors, that is why they teach them to do this, this is something they do not know, and even if they knew, they could not sympathize with it.

Combining the above reasons, it is simply impossible to prevent the decline of the teacher's position! Children are the pillars of the future country, and teachers have the responsibility to make this pillar firm. Since teachers bear a heavy responsibility, they should not be despised by others. This has become a natural and righteous principle. As for the teacher's own cultivation, that is also important. Teachers are the ideal object for children, and every move of the teacher can affect the child's behavior. Teachers' words and deeds should be consistent. If they say something, they should do it. Only in this way can they gain the faith of children, make teaching easier, and only in this way can the education career have hope of dawn.

Attention Unemployed Friends

Scientific Miscellany

The Story of the Invention of the Airship for Saving the Country Through Aviation (3)

— Shulin

In 1766, the famous British chemist Cavendish discovered hydrogen, which is much lighter than air. This was a major revolution in the world of balloons.

After that, Dr. Edenburg Pollock began to make balloons filled with hydrogen. The doctor put hydrogen into ox intestines, but failed due to excessive weight. After the discovery of hydrogen, no one used it for a while.

After several years, the French Montgolfier brothers experimented with making balloons. The elder brother was named Stanford, and the younger brother was named Joshua. They originally worked in a paper shop in the Annonay district and accidentally came up with the idea of making balloons. Interestingly, the invention of balloons and airplanes was often successful due to the cooperation of brothers. The invention of the Zeppelin airship by Zeppelin and his brother Haberth, and the invention of the Wright airplane, are all facts of successful cooperation between brothers. The Montgolfier brothers thought that they could make a large bag with many pieces of paper and fill it with smoke to rise into the sky.

The brothers discussed and made a large paper bag, which was extremely convenient in the paper shop. They took the bag to the center of the courtyard and lit dry grass under it.

The brothers laughed happily. The paper bag filled with smoke and left the brothers' hands and rose. They looked up and sat down, clapping and cheering. They were naturally happy that their design had been successful. But at that time, the bag did not rise because it was filled with smoke, but because it was heated by the air and became lighter, it was carried up.

Then the Montgolfier brothers made a second large balloon, which expanded into a circle with a diameter of 30 feet.

On June 5, 1783, this balloon was scheduled to be released in Annonay Square. Thousands of people gathered after hearing the news. Montgolfier's balloon rose quietly towards the clear space. The audience cheered in unison, and the brothers' elation can be imagined. As a result, it undoubtedly achieved great success at the time. The balloon rose one and a half miles, and after the air inside gradually cooled, it slowly descended.

Montgolfier's balloon at that time, of course, could not carry cargo or passengers.

The success of the brothers gave everyone a great stimulus, and the number of people manufacturing balloons suddenly increased. In August of that year, the famous scientist Aim, Quers and the Robert brothers made a balloon. The outer skin of the balloon was made of thin silk coated with rubber, and it was filled with hydrogen. (To be continued)
